# Product Requirements Document (PRD)
## Addiction Recovery App - "Regal Recovery"

**Document Version:** 2.0
**Last Updated:** March 29, 2026
**Product Manager:** [Your Name]
**Target Launch:** TBD

---

## 1. Executive Summary/Purpose

### 1.1 Why Are We Building This?

**The Problem:**
Sexual addiction, often co-occurring with multiple other addictive behaviors, affects millions of individuals and their families. Current recovery solutions are fragmented—requiring users to juggle multiple apps, journals, meeting schedules, and support networks. Those seeking recovery from a Christian perspective face an additional challenge: most secular recovery apps lack spiritual integration, while faith-based resources often lack the sophisticated digital tools necessary for daily accountability and progress tracking.

**The Opportunity:**
We are building Regal Recovery to provide a comprehensive, integrated recovery platform that addresses the whole person—mentally, intellectually, physically, emotionally, and spiritually—from a Christian worldview. This app will serve as a "digital recovery companion" that combines evidence-based addiction recovery methodologies with Christian discipleship, community accountability, and intelligent tracking.

**Business Objectives:**
- Establish market leadership in faith-based addiction recovery technology
- Achieve 50,000 active users
- Create sustainable revenue through freemium model with premium content partnerships
- Build a supportive community that reduces isolation and increases recovery success rates
- Develop partnerships with Christian counseling organizations and recovery ministries

**Success Definition:**
Users will experience increased sobriety duration, reduced relapse frequency, improved mental health metrics, and strengthened spiritual practices, supported by measurable engagement with daily tools and community features.

---

## 2. Target Audience

### 2.1 Primary Audience

**Core User Profile:**
- **Demographics:** Males and females, ages 18-65, predominantly 25-45
- **Geographic:** English and Spanish-speaking regions (US, Canada, UK, Australia, Mexico, and Latin America initially)
- **Faith Background:** Christians (all denominations) seeking faith-integrated recovery
- **Addiction Profile:** Primary sex addiction with common co-addictions (pornography, substance use, gambling, shopping, eating disorders)
- **Recovery Stage:** All stages—from pre-contemplation to long-term maintenance
- **Tech Proficiency:** Moderate to high; comfortable with smartphone apps and digital tools
- **Economic Status:** Middle income; willing to pay for premium resources that support recovery

### 2.2 Secondary Audiences

1. **Spouses/Partners:** Individuals supporting someone in recovery, needing their own tools and education
2. **Sponsors/Accountability Partners:** Mentors providing guidance and oversight
3. **Therapists/Counselors:** Licensed professionals managing client recovery through the platform
4. **Recovery Coaches:** Certified coaches coordinating recovery activities
5. **Ministry Leaders:** Church and para-church organization staff facilitating group recovery programs

### 2.3 User Segmentation

- **Segment A - Early Recovery (0-90 days):** High risk, needs intensive daily tools and accountability
- **Segment B - Active Recovery (90 days - 2 years):** Building habits, needs structure and milestone tracking
- **Segment C - Maintenance (2+ years):** Sustained sobriety, needs community and ongoing growth tools
- **Segment D - Multi-Addiction:** Complex recovery needs requiring multiple tracking systems
- **Segment E - Couples in Recovery:** Both individual and relational healing needs

---

## 3. User Personas & Pain Points

### 3.1 Primary Persona: "Addict Alex"

**Demographics:**
- Age: 34
- Occupation: IT Project Manager
- Location: Suburban Dallas, TX
- Marital Status: Married to Sarah, 2 children (ages 4 and 7)
- Faith: Evangelical Christian, attends church regularly
- Recovery Stage: Early recovery (45 days sober)

**Background:**
Alex has struggled with pornography and sex addiction for 15 years. After his wife Sarah discovered his behavior, he committed to recovery. He attends a weekly 12-step meeting, sees a Christian therapist bi-weekly, and has a sponsor (Sam) in his recovery group. He's motivated but overwhelmed by managing recovery alongside work and family demands.

**Goals:**
- Maintain daily sobriety and rebuild trust with his wife
- Develop healthy coping mechanisms for stress and triggers
- Integrate his faith meaningfully into recovery
- Track progress and celebrate milestones
- Connect with others who understand his struggle

**Pain Points:**
- **Fragmented Tools:** Uses paper journals, separate tracking apps, and scattered resources
- **Trigger Vulnerability:** Experiences sudden urges with no immediate intervention tool
- **Shame & Isolation:** Feels alone in his struggle, fears judgment from church community
- **Accountability Gaps:** Struggles to maintain daily consistency without external accountability
- **Spiritual Disconnect:** Finds it hard to connect scripture and prayer to practical recovery
- **Time Constraints:** Limited time for recovery work between job and family responsibilities
- **Relapse Fear:** Anxious about slip-ups and doesn't have a structured relapse prevention plan
- **Partner Relationship:** Doesn't know how to involve his wife appropriately in his recovery

**Technology Behaviors:**
- Uses iPhone 13, Apple Watch
- Active on limited social media (deleted Instagram due to triggers)
- Prefers apps with clean, simple interfaces
- Uses voice-to-text frequently while commuting
- Values privacy and security features

**Quote:** *"I want to get better, but I feel like I'm juggling ten different things and nothing fits together. I need something that helps me stay focused every single day and reminds me why I'm doing this."*

---

### 3.2 Secondary Persona: "Spouse Sarah"

**Demographics:**
- Age: 32
- Occupation: Elementary School Teacher
- Location: Suburban Dallas, TX
- Marital Status: Married to Alex
- Faith: Evangelical Christian
- Role: Betrayed spouse seeking healing

**Background:**
Sarah discovered Alex's addiction 6 months ago. She's devastated but committed to their marriage and recovery journey. She attends a betrayal trauma support group and sees her own therapist. She wants to support Alex while also protecting her own emotional health.

**Goals:**
- Understand Alex's recovery without enabling
- Heal from betrayal trauma
- Establish healthy boundaries
- Regain trust through transparency
- Connect with other spouses in similar situations

**Pain Points:**
- **Trust Issues:** Needs visibility into recovery but doesn't want to be a "recovery cop"
- **Emotional Overload:** Processing her own trauma while supporting Alex
- **Information Gap:** Doesn't fully understand addiction mechanics and recovery process
- **Boundary Confusion:** Unsure what level of involvement is healthy
- **Isolation:** Feels alone and embarrassed about the situation
- **Safety Concerns:** Wants to know if Alex is maintaining sobriety without micromanaging

**Technology Behaviors:**
- Uses iPhone 12
- Active on Pinterest, Facebook groups for support
- Values secure, private communication
- Prefers receiving updates via notifications

**Quote:** *"I want to believe he's changing, but I need to see it. I also need my own space to heal without constantly wondering if he's okay."*

---

### 3.3 Tertiary Persona: "Coach Caleb"

**Demographics:**
- Age: 45
- Occupation: Certified Recovery Coach
- Location: Fort Worth, TX
- Marital Status: Married, 2 teenage children
- Faith: Non-denominational Christian, active in recovery ministry
- Recovery Stage: 8 years sober, certified recovery coach

**Background:**
Caleb has been in recovery for 8 years and became a certified recovery coach 3 years ago. He works with both men and women in recovery, managing a caseload of 6-8 clients at any time. He partners with therapists and sponsors to provide holistic support but struggles to coordinate across all the people involved in each client's recovery.

**Goals:**
- Effectively coach multiple clients simultaneously with clear progress visibility
- Coordinate with each client's broader support team (therapist, sponsor, spouse)
- Provide timely encouragement and accountability between sessions
- Track clients' progress and identify warning signs early
- Share resources and assignments efficiently

**Pain Points:**
- **Communication Overload:** Receives texts/calls at all hours from different clients
- **Progress Tracking:** Hard to maintain a clear picture of each person's recovery trajectory
- **Coordination Gap:** No single place to see what the therapist assigned vs. what the sponsor recommended
- **Resource Sharing:** Manually sends articles, scripture, and tools repeatedly
- **Availability Limits:** Can't always respond immediately during crisis moments
- **Engagement Uncertainty:** Doesn't know if clients are doing their recovery work between sessions

**Technology Behaviors:**
- Uses Android Samsung Galaxy
- Moderate to high tech adoption, uses scheduling and note-taking apps
- Likes dashboard views that show key information quickly
- Values tools that reduce administrative overhead

**Quote:** *"I can see the progress my clients are making, but I wish I had a single place to track everything and coordinate with their sponsors and therapists without endless group texts."*

---

### 3.4 Quaternary Persona: "Sponsor Sam"

**Demographics:**
- Age: 52
- Occupation: Small Business Owner
- Location: Fort Worth, TX
- Marital Status: Married, 3 adult children
- Faith: Baptist, recovery ministry leader
- Recovery Stage: 12 years sober, active 12-step sponsor
- Relationship: Alex's 12-step sponsor

**Background:**
Sam has been in recovery for 12 years and sponsors 4 men in his SA group, including Alex. He's passionate about walking alongside men in their recovery journey and takes his role seriously. He meets with each sponsee weekly but struggles to keep track of everyone's progress between meetings. He volunteers with his church's recovery ministry on weekends.

**Goals:**
- Walk sponsees through the 12 steps with consistent accountability
- Respond quickly when a sponsee is in crisis
- Track each sponsee's progress and identify warning signs
- Share step work assignments and recovery literature efficiently
- Maintain healthy boundaries while being available

**Pain Points:**
- **Juggling Multiple Sponsees:** Hard to remember where each person is in their step work
- **Crisis Availability:** Can't always answer the phone when someone needs help at 2 AM
- **Progress Visibility:** Relies on sponsees' self-reporting, which may not tell the full picture
- **Communication Scatter:** Uses text, phone calls, and in-person meetings with no central record
- **Resource Repetition:** Keeps sending the same readings and assignments manually to different sponsees

**Technology Behaviors:**
- Uses Android Samsung Galaxy
- Low-moderate tech adoption, prefers simple interfaces
- Uses email and text primarily
- Would value a dashboard showing sponsees' status at a glance

**Quote:** *"I love helping these guys, but I wish I had a better way to stay connected and see how they're really doing day-to-day without being intrusive."*

---

### 3.5 Primary Persona: "Addict Allison"

**Demographics:**
- Age: 29
- Occupation: Marketing Coordinator
- Location: Austin, TX
- Marital Status: Married to Sam (Spouse Sam), no children
- Faith: Catholic, exploring deeper relationship with God through recovery
- Recovery Stage: Pre-recovery / contemplation (recently acknowledged the problem)

**Background:**
Allison has struggled with compulsive sexual behavior and emotional affairs for 6 years. She recently confessed to her husband Sam after a particularly painful acting-out episode. She's seeing a Christian counselor (Claire) and is considering attending a women's 12-step group. As a woman dealing with sex addiction, she feels even more isolated than male counterparts due to societal stigma that this is "a man's problem."

**Goals:**
- Find a safe space where women with sex addiction are understood
- Build a recovery plan that integrates her Catholic faith
- Develop emotional awareness and healthy coping mechanisms
- Rebuild trust with her husband Sam
- Connect with a female sponsor who understands her experience

**Pain Points:**
- **Gender Stigma:** Most recovery resources and communities are male-focused; feels invisible
- **Shame Amplified:** Societal expectation that women don't struggle with sex addiction intensifies shame
- **Limited Female Resources:** Difficulty finding women's recovery groups, female sponsors, and female-authored content
- **Emotional Complexity:** Addiction is deeply intertwined with attachment wounds and emotional needs
- **Faith Confusion:** Feels unworthy of God's love; struggles to reconcile Catholic teaching with her behavior
- **Relationship Devastation:** Her husband is deeply hurt and she doesn't know how to support him while getting help herself
- **Privacy Fears:** Terrified that anyone at work or church will find out

**Technology Behaviors:**
- Uses iPhone 15, Apple Watch
- Active on TikTok and Reddit (lurks in recovery communities anonymously)
- Prefers apps with strong privacy features and anonymous modes
- Comfortable with technology, expects modern UX

**Quote:** *"I didn't even know women could have this problem. When I finally admitted it, I couldn't find anyone who understood. Everything out there is for men. I need help, but I need to feel safe first."*

---

### 3.6 Secondary Persona: "Spouse Sam"

**Demographics:**
- Age: 31
- Occupation: Software Engineer
- Location: Austin, TX
- Marital Status: Married to Allison
- Faith: Catholic, questioning
- Role: Betrayed spouse seeking understanding

**Background:**
Sam learned about Allison's addiction 2 months ago when she confessed. He's devastated, confused, and angry. As a male betrayed spouse of a female addict, he feels doubly isolated — most betrayed spouse resources assume the addict is male and the spouse is female. He's started individual therapy but hasn't found a support group that fits his situation.

**Goals:**
- Understand what sex addiction means and why Allison did what she did
- Process his own trauma without losing himself in her recovery
- Determine whether the marriage can survive and what that requires
- Find other men who are betrayed spouses (extremely rare community)
- Establish boundaries while remaining open to healing

**Pain Points:**
- **Role Reversal Isolation:** Almost no resources for male betrayed spouses; feels like he doesn't exist in the recovery world
- **Stigma & Embarrassment:** Embarrassed to tell anyone his wife has a sex addiction
- **Anger & Confusion:** Swings between wanting to support Allison and wanting to leave
- **Information Void:** Doesn't understand the difference between addiction and deliberate betrayal
- **Boundary Confusion:** Doesn't know what healthy involvement in her recovery looks like
- **Trust Shattered:** Wants transparency but doesn't know what to ask for

**Technology Behaviors:**
- Uses iPhone 14 Pro
- Tech-savvy, comfortable with complex apps
- Values data and metrics (wants to see concrete progress)
- Prefers text-based communication over phone calls

**Quote:** *"Nobody talks about this from the man's side. When I try to explain what happened, people either don't believe me or tell me I should just leave. I need someone who gets it."*

---

### 3.7 Tertiary Persona: "Counselor Claire"

**Demographics:**
- Age: 41
- Occupation: Licensed Professional Counselor (LPC), CSAT (Certified Sex Addiction Therapist)
- Location: Austin, TX
- Marital Status: Married
- Faith: Non-denominational Christian
- Role: Allison's therapist, also treats other clients through the platform

**Background:**
Claire is a licensed counselor specializing in sex addiction with 12 years of experience. She sees 20+ clients weekly and uses a combination of CBT, EMDR, and faith-integrated approaches. She works with both male and female addicts and their partners. She currently juggles multiple tools for client communication, homework tracking, and progress notes and wishes she had a single integrated platform.

**Goals:**
- Monitor clients' recovery progress between sessions efficiently
- Assign therapeutic homework and track completion
- Coordinate with clients' sponsors and coaches when appropriate
- Access crisis alerts if a client is in danger
- Maintain professional boundaries while being responsive

**Pain Points:**
- **Tool Fragmentation:** Uses separate systems for scheduling, notes, client communication, and homework
- **Between-Session Blind Spots:** Only knows what clients self-report in weekly sessions
- **Crisis Response:** No way to know if a client is in crisis until they reach out directly
- **Coordination Gaps:** Can't easily communicate with a client's sponsor or coach about shared goals
- **Content Curation:** Spends time manually finding and sharing relevant articles, worksheets, and devotionals
- **Compliance Burden:** Needs tools that respect therapeutic boundaries and data privacy requirements

**Technology Behaviors:**
- Uses MacBook Pro and iPhone, iPad for sessions
- Uses EHR (Electronic Health Records) system for clinical notes
- Comfortable with professional SaaS tools
- Values HIPAA-adjacent data security and clear role-based access controls

**Quote:** *"My clients do the hardest work in between sessions, not during them. If I could see how they're actually doing day-to-day and step in when they need me, outcomes would be so much better."*

**Counselor/Therapist Platform Features:**

- **Profile:** Public-facing profile including Name, Website, Phone, and a Public About section — allowing users to discover and learn about counselors within the platform
- **Content:**
  - **Freemium Content:** Counselors can publish free articles, worksheets, devotionals, and psychoeducational resources available to all users as part of the resources library
  - **Premium Content:** Counselors can create gated content (e.g., structured courses, in-depth guides, specialized worksheets) available to subscribers or paying users as part of the premium resources library

---

### 3.8 Quaternary Persona: "Sponsor Sally"

**Demographics:**
- Age: 48
- Occupation: School Principal
- Location: San Antonio, TX
- Marital Status: Divorced, 2 children (college-age)
- Faith: Methodist, active in women's recovery ministry
- Recovery Stage: 10 years sober, sponsors 3 women
- Relationship: Allison's 12-step sponsor

**Background:**
Sally has been in recovery from sex and love addiction for 10 years. She's one of few women willing to sponsor other women in SA, which makes her highly sought after. She currently sponsors 3 women including Allison. Her own journey through addiction, divorce, and rebuilding her life gives her deep empathy but she sometimes struggles with compassion fatigue. She's committed to making the path easier for women who come after her.

**Goals:**
- Support her sponsees through step work with consistency and care
- Help normalize women's sex addiction recovery and reduce stigma
- Provide a safe, judgment-free relationship for vulnerable women
- Track sponsees' engagement without being overbearing
- Share female-specific recovery resources that are hard to find elsewhere

**Pain Points:**
- **High Demand, Low Supply:** One of very few female SA sponsors; frequently asked to take on more sponsees than she can handle
- **Resource Scarcity:** Most recovery literature and tools are written from a male perspective
- **Emotional Weight:** Sponsees' stories often trigger her own trauma; needs boundaries
- **Scheduling Chaos:** Hard to coordinate calls and check-ins across 3 sponsees and a demanding career
- **Visibility Gap:** Only knows how sponsees are doing when they call; wishes she could see daily engagement

**Technology Behaviors:**
- Uses iPhone 13
- Moderate tech adoption, appreciates well-designed apps
- Uses calendar apps and reminders extensively
- Values simplicity; will abandon tools that feel like extra work

**Quote:** *"Women in this recovery space are invisible. I sponsor because I know what it's like to have no one who understands. But I'm only one person — I need tools that help me be present for these women without burning out."*

---

### 3.9 Primary Persona: "Addict Marcus" — Single Male

**Demographics:**
- Age: 27
- Occupation: Electrician (union apprentice)
- Location: Charlotte, NC
- Marital Status: Single, never married; ended a 3-year relationship 8 months ago due to his addiction
- Faith: Non-denominational Christian, attends a small church plant irregularly
- Recovery Stage: Early recovery (21 days sober)
- Living Situation: Lives alone in a one-bedroom apartment

**Background:**
Marcus has struggled with pornography since age 13 and compulsive sexual behavior since college. His ex-girlfriend Keisha ended their relationship after discovering the extent of his addiction — a loss that finally pushed him to seek help. He started attending a Celebrate Recovery group at a church across town (not his own church — he's too ashamed to go to his home church's group). He doesn't have a sponsor yet and isn't seeing a therapist due to cost. His primary support is his CR group and his older brother Darren, who knows about the addiction but doesn't fully understand it.

Marcus's recovery is complicated by the fact that he lives alone with no built-in accountability structure. Evenings and weekends are his most dangerous times. Without a spouse or family at home, there's no external check on his behavior — if he relapses, no one knows unless he tells them. His social life has shrunk since the breakup, and most of his friends still consume pornography casually, which makes it hard to talk about his struggle without being dismissed.

**Goals:**
- Build a recovery life without a partner to hold him accountable — learn to be accountable to himself and God
- Find a sponsor who understands what it's like to be single in recovery
- Develop a healthy social life that doesn't revolve around dating, drinking, or digital consumption
- Process the grief of losing Keisha without using it as an excuse to relapse
- Afford professional help (therapy, recovery resources) on an apprentice's income
- Eventually become someone capable of a healthy relationship — but not rush into one

**Pain Points:**
- **No Built-In Accountability:** Lives alone — no spouse, no roommate, no one to notice if he disappears into his addiction for a weekend
- **Evening & Weekend Vulnerability:** Long, unstructured hours alone in his apartment are his highest-risk periods; the app needs to be especially useful during these windows
- **Financial Barriers:** Can't afford weekly therapy ($150/session); needs the app to fill the gap between free CR meetings and professional help he can't access
- **Social Isolation:** Lost his girlfriend and most of his social circle; rebuilding community from scratch while sober is daunting
- **Stigma Among Peers:** His male friends normalize pornography; talking about addiction feels like overreacting to them
- **No Spousal Features Needed — But Feels Excluded:** Much of the recovery content he encounters (apps, books, groups) assumes he's married and focuses on rebuilding trust with a spouse — he needs content for single men rebuilding themselves
- **Sponsor Gap:** Hasn't found a sponsor; nervous about asking someone; needs the app to provide some of the structure a sponsor would until he finds one
- **Dating Temptation:** Struggles with the urge to use dating apps as a substitute for genuine connection; needs tools to recognize when he's acting out relationally, not just sexually

**Technology Behaviors:**
- Uses Samsung Galaxy A54 (mid-range Android)
- Heavy smartphone user — phone is his primary entertainment device, which is also his primary trigger device
- Uses YouTube, Reddit, and Twitch extensively
- Comfortable with apps but won't pay for them unless he sees immediate value
- Values simplicity — will stop using anything that feels like extra work after a long shift

**Quote:** *"Everyone talks about rebuilding your marriage. I don't have a marriage. I barely have a friend group anymore. I need help figuring out how to be a whole person on my own before I can even think about being with someone else."*

**App Design Implications:**
- Content personalization for single users: Motivations, affirmations, and devotionals should include options that don't assume a spouse exists
- Evening/weekend engagement: The app should offer heightened engagement options during high-risk hours
- Affordable premium path: The freemium tier must deliver real value
- Sponsor-lite features: For users without a sponsor, the app should provide structure that partially fills the role
- Friendship and community beyond couples: Community features should support connection between single users in recovery
- Device as trigger awareness: Content or tools that help Marcus establish healthy phone boundaries

---

### 3.10 Primary Persona: "Addict Jasmine" — Single Female

**Demographics:**
- Age: 24
- Occupation: Graduate student (MSW — Master of Social Work)
- Location: Nashville, TN
- Marital Status: Single, dating casually (which is part of the problem)
- Faith: AME (African Methodist Episcopal), raised in the church, currently questioning but still attending
- Recovery Stage: Pre-recovery / early contemplation (3 days since she decided to get help)
- Living Situation: Lives with two roommates who don't know about her addiction

**Background:**
Jasmine has struggled with compulsive sexual behavior and love addiction for 5 years. Her pattern involves cycling through intense, short-lived sexual relationships and using dating apps compulsively — swiping, matching, and seeking validation through sexual attention. She recognized it as an addiction 6 months ago during a psychology class on behavioral addictions, but it took a pregnancy scare and a particularly degrading encounter to push her toward help.

As a young Black woman in the church, Jasmine faces layers of stigma. Her church culture doesn't openly discuss sex addiction — it barely discusses sex at all. She's terrified of being judged as promiscuous rather than understood as addicted. She's also studying to be a social worker, which makes her acutely aware of the clinical dimensions of her behavior but also makes her feel like she "should know better," compounding her shame.

She found Regal Recovery through a Reddit thread. She hasn't told anyone about her addiction — not her roommates, not her mother, not her pastor. She's considering finding a therapist but hasn't made the call yet.

**Goals:**
- Acknowledge and name her addiction without being crushed by shame
- Find other women — especially women of color — who understand compulsive sexual behavior and love addiction
- Develop healthy relationship patterns and learn to be alone without seeking validation through sexual attention
- Reconcile her faith with her behavior — she feels like a hypocrite sitting in church on Sunday after her Saturday nights
- Build a recovery plan she can follow while managing graduate school, clinical placements, and a social life
- Eventually tell someone she trusts — but she's not ready yet and needs the app to be her first safe space

**Pain Points:**
- **Total Secrecy:** No one in her life knows. The gap between her public image and private behavior is destroying her from the inside.
- **Love Addiction Overlap:** Her addiction isn't just about sex — it's about the pursuit of romantic intensity, the validation of being desired, and the inability to tolerate emotional aloneness. Most sex addiction tools focus on pornography and don't address love/relationship addiction
- **Cultural & Racial Isolation:** Almost no recovery resources speak to her experience as a young Black woman. Recovery spaces are predominantly white and male.
- **Church Silence:** Her church doesn't talk about sex addiction. Purity culture messaging makes her feel dirty, not helped.
- **Dating App Compulsion:** Her phone is her primary acting-out tool — not through pornography but through dating apps
- **Graduate School Stress:** Intense academic pressure and emotional labor from clinical placements create constant stress — a primary trigger
- **Age & Stage:** At 24, she's younger than most recovery personas. Recovery advice that assumes a settled, married adult doesn't translate to her life.
- **Professional Identity Conflict:** She's studying to help others with mental health challenges while secretly struggling with her own.

**Technology Behaviors:**
- Uses iPhone 15
- Heavy social media user — Instagram, TikTok, Twitter/X, dating apps
- Expects polished, modern UX — will judge the app by its design quality within seconds
- Uses her phone as her journal (Notes app) and therapist (Reddit lurking)
- Values anonymity features above all else
- Consumes content via audio (podcasts, audiobooks) during commutes and workouts

**Quote:** *"I know what this is clinically. I can name the attachment wounds, the dopamine cycle, all of it. But knowing doesn't stop me from doing it. I need something that helps me in the moment — at 11 PM on a Friday when I'm about to open Hinge again — not another article about brain chemistry."*

**App Design Implications:**
- Love addiction and relationship addiction content: The app should address compulsive relationship-seeking, validation addiction, and emotional dependency
- Anonymous-first experience: The app should function fully without connecting to any support network
- Representation in content: Devotionals, affirmations, and imagery should reflect diverse racial and ethnic backgrounds
- Dating app trigger tools: Urge logging and emergency tools should include dating app compulsion as a recognized trigger category
- Audio-first content options: Devotionals, affirmations, and prayers with TTS or recorded audio support
- Younger user UX expectations: The app's design quality needs to meet the standard set by consumer apps she uses daily
- Pre-support-network value: The app must deliver its full value for a user who has zero support contacts configured

---

### 3.11 Primary Persona: "Addict Diego" — Spanish-Speaking

**Demographics:**
- Age: 38
- Occupation: Construction foreman
- Location: Houston, TX (originally from Monterrey, Mexico; moved to the US 12 years ago)
- Marital Status: Married to Lucia, 3 children (ages 6, 9, and 12)
- Faith: Catholic, attends Mass weekly, active in his parish's men's group
- Recovery Stage: Early recovery (30 days sober)
- Language: Spanish-dominant bilingual — speaks English at work but thinks, prays, and processes emotions in Spanish
- Living Situation: Family home in a predominantly Hispanic neighborhood

**Background:**
Diego has struggled with pornography and visits to massage parlors for 10 years. His wife Lucia discovered his behavior 2 months ago when she found charges on their credit card. The revelation has devastated their marriage and shaken their family. Diego is deeply ashamed — in his culture and community, a man's sexual behavior is rarely discussed, and addiction is seen as a lack of willpower or faith rather than a treatable condition.

Diego confessed to his parish priest, who was compassionate but didn't know how to help beyond prayer and confession. The priest referred him to a Catholic counseling center, where he's been seeing a bilingual therapist (Dr. Reyes) bi-weekly. Diego also found a Spanish-language SA meeting that meets weekly — one of only two Spanish-language SA meetings in the greater Houston area.

Diego's English is functional for work but not for emotional processing. When he tried an English-language recovery app, he understood the words but couldn't connect with them — reading affirmations in English felt like reading a manual, not hearing God speak to him. He needs recovery tools in Spanish — not just translated Spanish, but culturally resonant Spanish that reflects his Catholic faith, his Mexican cultural context, and the way he actually thinks and prays.

**Goals:**
- Get sober and stay sober — for his children, his marriage, and his relationship with God
- Find recovery resources in Spanish that don't feel like afterthoughts or machine translations
- Rebuild trust with Lucia — she's considering separation
- Process shame in a culturally safe context — machismo culture makes admitting sexual weakness feel impossible
- Connect with other Spanish-speaking men in recovery
- Integrate his Catholic faith into recovery — he needs sacramental language alongside 12-step language

**Pain Points:**
- **Language as a Barrier to Healing:** English-language recovery content doesn't reach him emotionally. He can read it, but he can't feel it.
- **Cultural Stigma (Machismo):** Admitting sexual addiction is seen as admitting weakness, deviance, or moral failure in his cultural context
- **Catholic-Specific Faith Integration:** Most Christian recovery apps lean evangelical/Protestant. Diego needs content that resonates with Catholic spirituality — the sacraments, the saints, the Rosary, confession and reconciliation, Marian devotion
- **Scarcity of Spanish-Language Recovery Community:** Very few Spanish-language SA meetings or online communities
- **Family Financial Pressure:** Therapy costs are straining the family budget
- **Work Schedule Constraints:** 10-12 hour days on construction sites with early mornings. Recovery window is narrow.
- **Digital Literacy Gap:** Comfortable with WhatsApp and YouTube but not a power user. Complex app navigation will go unused.
- **Spousal Relationship in Crisis:** Lucia is hurt, angry, and considering leaving.

**Technology Behaviors:**
- Uses Samsung Galaxy A14 (budget Android)
- Primary apps: WhatsApp, YouTube, Facebook
- Prefers voice input over typing — especially for journaling in Spanish
- Low tolerance for complexity — if he can't figure out a feature in 30 seconds, he'll skip it
- Data plan conscious — avoids features that consume large amounts of data

**Quote:** *"Cuando intento leer las afirmaciones en inglés, las entiendo pero no las siento. Necesito escuchar la verdad de Dios en mi idioma — en el idioma en que rezo, en que lloro, en que le pido perdón."*

Translation: *"When I try to read the affirmations in English, I understand them but I don't feel them. I need to hear God's truth in my language — the language I pray in, I cry in, I ask for forgiveness in."*

**App Design Implications:**
- Spanish as a first-class experience, not a translation layer: culturally adapted affirmations and prayers, established Spanish Bible translations (RVR1960, Biblia Latinoamericana), recovery terminology reviewed by Spanish-speaking professionals
- Catholic content track: prayers to the saints, Rosary-based meditations, Ignatian Examen, confession preparation tools, Theology of the Body references
- Voice-first input: Voice-to-text must work well in Mexican Spanish
- Simple, clear navigation: features discoverable in 1-2 taps, large tap targets, icons with text labels
- Low data consumption mode: downloadable content for offline use, audio-only alternatives for video
- WhatsApp integration consideration for accountability broadcasts and support network notifications
- Community matching by language for accountability partner and community features
- Spousal features that work without the spouse using the app: PDF exports, screenshot-friendly milestone cards

---

### 3.12 Pain Point Matrix

| User Persona | Emotional Pain | Practical Pain | Spiritual Pain | Relational Pain |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Addict Alex** | Shame, anxiety, fear of failure | Disorganized tools, time management | Faith feels disconnected from recovery | Broken trust with spouse |
| **Spouse Sarah** | Trauma, distrust, fear | Information gap, boundary confusion | Anger at God, faith shaken | Communication breakdown |
| **Coach Caleb** | Compassion fatigue | Coordination across support teams, time limits | Feeling inadequate as spiritual guide | Limited connection depth with clients |
| **Sponsor Sam** | Worry for sponsees, emotional weight | Tracking multiple sponsees manually | Desire to be a better spiritual mentor | Boundaries with sponsees' families |
| **Addict Allison** | Amplified shame, gender stigma | No female-specific tools or communities | Feels unworthy of God's love | Devastated husband, fear of exposure |
| **Spouse Sam** | Anger, confusion, isolation | No male betrayed-spouse resources | Questioning faith and fairness | Role reversal with no roadmap |
| **Counselor Claire** | Vicarious trauma, helplessness between sessions | Tool fragmentation, no integrated view | Balancing clinical and spiritual approaches | Professional boundary management |
| **Sponsor Sally** | Compassion fatigue, over-demand | Scarcity of female recovery resources | Carrying others' spiritual burdens | Managing boundaries with sponsees |
| **Addict Marcus** | Shame, loneliness, grief from lost relationship | No built-in accountability, financial barriers to therapy | Faith feels inconsistent, church attendance irregular | No spouse, shrinking social circle, no sponsor yet |
| **Addict Jasmine** | Deep secrecy, identity conflict, fear of exposure | No love addiction-specific tools, dating app compulsion | Hypocrisy guilt, church silence on sex, purity culture harm | Total isolation — no one knows; broken relationship patterns |
| **Addict Diego** | Machismo shame, fear of losing family | Language barrier in recovery tools, limited Spanish-language meetings, work schedule constraints | Needs Catholic-specific spiritual integration, sacramental language | Marriage in crisis, wife considering separation, children affected |

---

## 4. Key Features & Requirements

### 4.1 Feature Categories Overview

**1. Onboarding & Profile Setup** — Two-track onboarding (Fast Track + Deferred Profile Completion), language selection, role-based onboarding, personal recovery profile

**2. Profile Management** — Support network connections (sponsor, counselor, spouse, accountability partner)

**3. Tracking System** — Tracks both positive and negative behaviors
- Tracker Types:
  1. Counting Days Since Last Activity (sobriety)
  2. Counting Days of Consecutive Activity (commitments, affirmations, journaling, check-ins, custom)
- Activity Being Tracked: Sobriety, Commitments, Affirmations, Journaling, Check-ins, Custom
- Per Tracker Views: Current Streak, History of Lengths/Milestones, Calendar with History
- Aggregate View: All Current Streaks, Combined History, Calendar with All Activity

**4. Content/Resources System** — Provides content/resources for users
- Freemium: Basic Commitments Pack, Basic Affirmations Pack, Basic Devotionals, Partner Content
- Premium (unlocked forever when purchased): More Commitments Packs, More Affirmations Packs, Premium Partner Content, Premium Devotionals

**5. Commitments System** — Track personal recovery commitments
- Out-of-the-box commitments (daily check-ins, daily phone calls, daily/weekly meetings, etc.)
- Custom commitments: what is it? how often?

**6. Activities** — Activities a user can take
- Daily Sobriety Commitment
- Affirmations
- Urge Logging & Emergency Tools
- Journaling (bullets, free-form, prompted, structured)
- Emotional Journaling
- Recovery Check-ins
- Person Check-ins (Spouse, Sponsor, Counselor/Coach)
- Spouse Check-in Preparation (FANOS/FITNAP)
- Guided 12 Step Work
- Meetings Attended
- Personal Craziness Index (PCI)
- FASTER Scale
- Post-Mortem Analysis
- Financial Tracker
- Acting In Behaviors
- Weekly/Daily Goals
- Devotionals
- Exercise/Physical Activity
- Nutrition
- Mood Ratings
- Gratitude List
- Phone Calls (made and received)
- Prayer
- Partner Activities (Redemptive Living: T30/60 journaling, Emotional Journaling, Empathy exercises, Backbone, Bow Tie, Empathy Mapping, Threats)
- Voice Journal / Audio Entries

**7. Singular Static Tools**
- 3 Circles Tool — Visual mapping of inner/middle/outer circle behaviors
- Maintenance Plan
- Vision

**8. Notification Strategy** — Priority hierarchy, daily caps, intelligent batching, quiet hours

**9. Analytics Dashboard** — Trends and stats

**10. Premium Advanced Analytics Dashboard** — Deeper trends and recovery insights

**11. Recovery Chatbot** — AI-powered conversational support with crisis escalation

**12. Community**
- Roles: Spouse, Accountability Partner, Sponsor, Coach, Counselor, Member (all)
- Permissions: Reading, Commenting; other recommendations
- Viewing Permissions: by Role, by Category/Activity, by Item
- View addict's data on a per-permission basis (default: no access; individual, category, or activity-level grants)
- Defaults: Spouse/Counselor/Coach see all; Accountability Partner/Sponsor see all except journal and financial
- Messaging with Spouse, Accountability Partner, Sponsor, Coach, Counselor only

**13. Branding** — Brand the app via configuration for complete white-labeling in private partner contexts

**14. Tenancy**
- Every user is in the main tenant
- B2B (ministries, recovery centers, etc.) are their own tenants, leveraged for white-labeled instances

**15. Data Subject Rights (DSR)** — Export or delete all personal data

**16. Data Backup** — Backup data to iCloud, Google Drive, or Dropbox

**17. Quick Action Shortcuts** — OS-level shortcuts (Apple Action Button, Siri Shortcuts, Android App Shortcuts) for rapid access to key activities

**18. WebKit Content Filter Accountability** — On-device content filtering and screen accountability with AI classification and accountability reports to support contacts

**19. Panic Button with Biometric Awareness** — Enhanced emergency intervention using front-facing camera for self-awareness disruption and facial expression analysis for personalized intervention

**20. Therapist Portal** — Web-based dashboard for therapists/CSATs to manage clients, assign homework, monitor progress, and receive crisis alerts

**21. Guided Breathing and Grounding Exercises** — Purpose-built breathing and grounding exercises for urge interruption and emotional regulation

**22. Recovery Health Score** — Single holistic score (0-100) synthesizing all recovery data into a daily pulse check

**23. Achievement System and Gamification** — Milestone celebrations with digital sobriety coins, consistency achievements, content consumption gamification, and anonymous milestone sharing

**24. Superbill and LMN Generation** — In-app medical billing documents for HSA/FSA reimbursement and insurance submission

**25. Meeting Finder** — GPS-powered meeting search across SA, SAA, Celebrate Recovery, AA, and S-Anon with NextMeeting SA integration

**26. Messaging Integrations** — WhatsApp, Signal, and Telegram deep links for accountability broadcasts, support communications, and milestone sharing

**27. Offline-First Content and Low Data Mode** — Pre-downloadable content and reduced bandwidth mode for metered data plans

**28. Trigger-Based Geofencing** — Proactive location-aware recovery support with high-risk zone detection and safe zone recognition

**29. Screen Time and Digital Wellness** — iOS Screen Time / Android Digital Wellbeing integration with recovery-correlated insights and digital boundary tools

**30. Couples Recovery Mode** — Unified couples dashboard with shared goals, trust-rebuilding milestones, couples devotionals, communication exercises, and shared calendar

**31. Sleep Tracking Integration** — Apple Health / Google Fit sleep data with recovery correlation insights and poor-sleep risk alerts

**32. Voice Journal / Audio Entries** — Audio-first journaling preserving raw voice recordings alongside auto-generated transcripts

**33. Content Trigger Log** — Behavioral logging of user responses after content filter events for pattern analysis and Post-Mortem correlation

**34. Book Logging / Recovery Bookshelf** — Personal reading tracker with chapter notes, progress tracking, and stage-based recommendations

**35. Anonymous Recovery Stories** — Moderated library of user-submitted recovery testimonials filterable by addiction type, gender, stage, and faith background

**36. Assessment Tools** — Structured self-evaluation instruments including Family Impact Assessment, Denial Assessment, Addiction Severity Assessment, and Relationship Health Assessment

**37. Podcasts** — Curated recovery podcast directory with deep links to Apple Podcasts and Spotify

**38. External Links** — Vetted directory of recovery organizations, crisis hotlines, fellowships, and clinical resources

**39. Arousal Template** — Guided clinical tool based on Patrick Carnes' framework for understanding and reshaping sexual arousal patterns (therapist-recommended)

**40. Memory Verse Study and Quizzing** — Scripture memorization with verse packs, spaced repetition, and interactive quizzing in user's preferred Bible translation

**41. Spotify Integration** — In-app music playback control with activity-specific playlist suggestions and curated recovery playlists

**42. SAST-R (Sexual Addiction Screening Test)** — Validated 20-item clinical screening instrument by Patrick Carnes for baseline and periodic assessment

---

### 4.2 Detailed Feature Specifications

---

#### **FEATURE 1: Onboarding & Profile Setup**

**Priority:** P0 (Must-Have)

**Description:** Language selection, role-based onboarding, personal recovery profile creation, and progressive profile completion strategy designed to minimize drop-off while maximizing the data needed for a personalized recovery experience.

**Onboarding Philosophy:**

- **Speed to value:** Get the user to the Dashboard and their first meaningful recovery action as fast as possible.
- **Progressive disclosure:** Collect only what's essential upfront. Defer everything else to contextual moments.
- **Emotional safety:** Many users are downloading this app during a crisis. Onboarding must feel like a warm welcome, not an intake form.
- **No dead ends:** Every screen must have a clear path forward. Optional steps are always skippable.

**Two-Track Onboarding:**

1. **Fast Track (3-4 steps)** — Gets the user to the Dashboard in under 2 minutes. Collects only what's required to start using the app.
2. **Deferred Profile Completion** — Prompts the user to complete their profile over the first 7-14 days through contextual, in-app nudges tied to natural moments of engagement.

**User Stories:**
- As a **new user**, I want to start using the app as quickly as possible, so that I can get help right now instead of filling out a long form while I'm struggling
- As a **new user**, I want a welcoming experience that feels safe and compassionate, so that I don't feel judged or overwhelmed before I even start
- As a **new user**, I want to set my sobriety start date immediately, so that my streak begins tracking from day one
- As a **new user**, I want to complete my profile gradually over my first week, so that it doesn't feel like a barrier to getting started
- As a **new user**, I want the app to explain why it's asking for each piece of information, so that I trust that my data is being used to help me
- As a **new user**, I want to identify my primary addiction, so that the app shows me relevant tools and content from the start
- As a **new user**, I want to skip optional setup steps without guilt, so that I can return to them when I'm ready
- As a **new user in crisis**, I want to access emergency tools immediately, so that I can get help even before completing onboarding
- As a **returning user**, I want to pick up where I left off if I closed the app during onboarding, so that I don't have to start over
- As a **new user**, I want to be prompted to complete my profile at natural moments, so that finishing setup feels useful rather than arbitrary

**Fast Track Flow (Required — Under 2 Minutes):**

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start([App Launch]) --> Lang[1. Language Selection]
    Lang --> Welcome[2. Welcome Screen]
    Welcome --> SignIn{Existing account?}
    SignIn -- Yes --> Login([Sign In Flow])
    SignIn -- No --> Account[3. Account Creation]
    Account --> Core[4. Core Setup\nName, Primary Addiction,\nSobriety Date]
    Core --> Notif[5. Enable Notifications\nSingle permission prompt]
    Notif --> Dashboard([Go to Dashboard\n🎉 Welcome Animation])

    style Start fill:#4A90D9,color:#fff
    style Dashboard fill:#7ED321,color:#fff
    style Login fill:#4A90D9,color:#fff
```

**Step 1: Language Selection**
- Auto-detect device language setting
- Display options: "English" / "Español"
- Large, clear buttons with flag icons
- Selection applies immediately; can be changed later in Settings
- If device language is neither English nor Spanish, default to English

**Step 2: Welcome Screen**
- Headline: "You're not alone. And you're in the right place."
- Three brief value propositions (icon + one line each)
- Primary CTA: "Get Started"
- Secondary link: "Already have an account? Sign In"
- Crisis access: "Need help right now? Tap here" → opens Emergency Tools overlay immediately, no account required

**Step 3: Account Creation**
- Sign-up options: Email, Apple ID, Google
- Email flow with real-time validation
- Legal: single checkbox for Terms + Privacy Policy
- Email verification sent in background — user NOT blocked from proceeding
- Biometric opt-in prompt after account creation

**Step 4: Core Setup (Single Screen)**
- Display name (required, max 30 characters)
- Primary addiction (required, selection chips): Sex Addiction, Pornography, Substance Use, Gambling, Shopping, Eating Disorders, Other
- Sobriety start date (required, date picker, default: today)

**Step 5: Enable Notifications (Single Prompt)**
- Single, clear ask: "Can we send you a daily reminder to make your recovery commitment?"
- Primary CTA: "Enable Reminders" → triggers OS notification permission
- Secondary: "Not now" → skips; banner on Dashboard later

**Dashboard Arrival**
- Welcome animation with sobriety streak displayed prominently
- Three suggested first actions: Make first commitment, Read today's affirmation, Set up support network
- Profile completion banner with progress ring

**Deferred Profile Completion Strategy:**

Profile completion is woven into the app experience over the first 7-14 days. Each missing field is requested at the moment when it's most relevant.

| Profile Field | Fast Track? | Deferred Trigger |
|---|---|---|
| Display name | ✅ Required | — |
| Primary addiction | ✅ Required | — |
| Sobriety start date | ✅ Required | — |
| Birth year + Gender | ❌ | Day 2: After first morning commitment |
| Marital status | ❌ | Day 3: Before first spouse check-in prep |
| Time zone | ❌ (auto-detected) | Only if auto-detection fails |
| Co-addictions | ❌ | Day 3-5: After first urge log |
| Previous recovery history | ❌ | Day 5-7: After first milestone |
| Motivations | ❌ | Day 2-3: After first evening review |
| Support network setup | ❌ | Day 3-5: After first "I'm struggling" moment |
| Notification preferences (detailed) | ❌ | Day 4-7: After experiencing 3-4 notification types |
| App permissions | ❌ | Contextually, when feature requiring permission is first used |
| Faith background | ❌ | Day 5-7: After engaging with devotional or prayer content |

Each deferred prompt follows a consistent pattern: context line (why we're asking), value line (what it unlocks), input fields (1-3 max), Save button, and "Not now" skip link. If skipped twice, the prompt moves to Settings only and does not appear again.

**Profile Completion Gamification:**
- Progress ring in Settings → Profile (percentage with visual fill)
- Dashboard banner for first 14 days (dismissible)
- Completing sections unlocks tangible benefits (personalized content, milestone messaging, community matching)
- 80% completion milestone celebration
- 100% completion badge

**App Permissions Strategy — Ask at the Moment of Use:**

| Permission | When Requested | Feature That Triggers It |
|---|---|---|
| Notifications | Fast Track Step 5 | Core app experience |
| Microphone | First voice-to-text attempt | Journaling, urge logging |
| Contacts | First "Call Sponsor" tap | Emergency tools, support network |
| Calendar | First calendar integration use | Evening commitment review |
| Health Data | First Exercise/Nutrition sync | Exercise, Nutrition |
| Location | First "Find meetings nearby" | Meeting finder, emergency tools |

**Role-Based Onboarding:**
- Spouse: 3-step Fast Track → spouse-specific dashboard
- Sponsor/Accountability Partner: 3-step Fast Track → sponsee dashboard
- Counselor/Coach: 4-step Fast Track (includes professional profile) → client management dashboard

**Returning User & Re-Engagement:**
- Interrupted onboarding: auto-saved, resumes on next launch
- Lapsed user: push notifications at Day 3, 7, 14; email at Day 14, 30; no further outreach after Day 30
- Returning after lapse: "Welcome back" with sobriety date update prompt, no shame messaging

**Success Criteria:**
- Fast Track completion rate: 95%+
- Time to Dashboard: Median under 2 minutes
- Day 7 profile completion: 60% of active users at 50%+
- Day 14 profile completion: 50% of active users at 80%+
- Day 1 action rate: 80% complete at least one recovery action

---

#### **FEATURE 2: Profile Management**

**Priority:** P0

**Description:** Support network connections (sponsor, counselor, spouse, accountability partner).

**User Stories:**
- As a user, I want to manage my profile information (name, email, gender, marital status, time zone), so that the app stays relevant to my recovery journey
- As a user, I want to update my addictions and sobriety dates, so that tracking remains accurate
- As a user, I want to manage my support network (sponsor, counselor, coach, accountability partner, spouse), so that I can control who is connected to my recovery

**Summary:**
- Accessible via Settings → Profile
- Editable fields: Name, email, birth year, gender, photo, time zone
- Addiction management: Add/remove addictions, designate primary
- Sobriety date management: Update with reason/logging
- Support network: Add/remove sponsor, counselor, coach, accountability partner, spouse (with email invites)
- Privacy settings: Control who sees what data
- Account management: Change password, delete account (with confirmation and data export)

**Preferred Bible Version:**
- Set in Profile → Faith Settings → Preferred Bible Version
- Applies globally across all scripture-displaying features: affirmations, devotionals, prayers, memory verses, journal prompts, milestone celebrations
- Supported English translations: NIV (default), ESV, NLT, KJV, NASB, NKJV, CSB, The Message
- Supported Spanish translations: RVR1960 (default for Spanish), NVI, DHH, LBLA, Biblia Latinoamericana, Biblia de Jerusalén
- Catholic-recommended translations flagged for Catholic users: Biblia Latinoamericana, Biblia de Jerusalén, NABRE
- User can view any individual verse in an alternate translation without changing their global preference ("Compare translations" tap on any displayed verse)
- Translation preference synced across all devices

---

#### **FEATURE 3: Tracking System**

**Priority:** P0 (Must-Have)

**Description:** Tracks both positive and negative behaviors across all activities.

**User Stories:**
- As a **recovering user**, I want to see my current sobriety streak, so that I can visualize my progress and stay motivated
- As a **recovering user**, I want to track consecutive days of positive activities, so that I build recovery habits
- As a **recovering user**, I want to view my complete history including past relapses, so that I can learn from patterns and celebrate overall growth
- As a **recovering user**, I want to see a calendar view of all my recovery activity, so that I can quickly identify strong periods and vulnerable times
- As a **recovering user**, I want to celebrate milestone achievements, so that I feel recognized and encouraged

**Tracker Types:**

1. **Counting Days Since Last Activity** — Used for sobriety tracking
2. **Counting Days of Consecutive Activity** — Used for positive behaviors

**Activity Being Tracked:** Sobriety, Commitments, Affirmations, Journaling, Emotional Journaling, Check-ins, Person Check-ins, Meetings, Step Work, Exercise, Nutrition, Mood, Gratitude, Calls, Prayer, Custom

**Per Tracker Views:**
1. Current Streak with visual progress indicator toward next milestone
2. History of Lengths/Milestones as timeline visualization
3. Calendar with History (color-coded days per activity)

**Aggregate View:**
1. All Current Streaks dashboard
2. Combined History timeline
3. Calendar with All Activity overlay

**Milestone System:**
- Visual badges for milestones: 1 day, 3 days, 7 days, 14 days, 30 days, 60 days, 3 months, 4 months, 5 months, 6 months, 7 months, 8 months, 9 months, 10 months, 11 months, 1 year, 18 months, 2 years, 5 years, 10 years
- Milestone celebration flow: full-screen animation, congratulations, reflection prompt, share options
- Optional notification to support network

**Relapse Logging Flow:**
- Compassionate messaging throughout
- Date/Time picker, addiction specification, optional Post-Mortem prompt
- Automatically resets sobriety date; previous streak preserved in history
- Support network notification option
- Recovery action plan prompt

**Multi-Addiction Tracking:**
- Independent tracking per addiction
- Unified view option
- Primary addiction designation for main dashboard

**Edge Cases:**
- Multiple relapses in one day → Only resets streak once
- Sobriety date in the future → Validation error
- Milestone at midnight → Celebration triggers next morning
- Time zone changes → Streak based on user's "home" time zone
- Offline data sync conflict → Most recent change wins; conflict noted
- Accidental relapse log → Allow undo within 24 hours

---

#### **FEATURE 4: Content/Resources System**

**Priority:** P1

**Description:** Provides content and resources for users through freemium and premium tiers.

**User Stories:**
- As a recovering user, I want access to recovery literature, so that I can deepen my understanding
- As a recovering user, I want Christian devotionals, so that I can integrate faith into daily recovery
- As a recovering user, I want to find local meetings and events, so that I can connect with in-person support

**Freemium Content:**
- Basic Commitments Pack, Basic Affirmations Pack (50+), Basic Devotionals (30-day rotation), Basic Prayers Pack, Partner Content
- Meeting finder, crisis lines, feeling wheel, free courses, curated music playlist, video library (10 free videos)

**Premium Content (unlocked forever when purchased):**
- More Commitments Packs, More Affirmations Packs, Premium Partner Content, Premium Devotionals (365-day), Premium Prayer Packs

**Counselor/Therapist Content:**
- Freemium and premium content publishing by counselors

**Memory Verses and Verse Packs:**
- **Freemium Verse Packs:** Identity in Christ (10 verses), Temptation & Strength (12 verses), Freedom & Recovery (10 verses)
- **Premium Verse Packs (unlocked forever when purchased):** Shame & Forgiveness, Marriage & Restoration, Anxiety & Peace, Purity & Holiness, Hope & Perseverance, Surrender & Trust (10-15 verses each)
- Verses displayed in user's preferred Bible version (set in Profile → Faith Settings)
- Verse packs integrated with Memory Verse Study and Quizzing activity (see Activity: Memory Verse Study and Quizzing)

---

#### **FEATURE 5: Commitments System**

**Priority:** P1

**Description:** Track personal recovery commitments with out-of-the-box and custom options.

**User Stories:**
- As a recovering user, I want to define specific commitments beyond just sobriety, so that I can build a comprehensive recovery lifestyle
- As a recovering user, I want to review my commitments nightly, so that I maintain honesty and accountability
- As a recovering user, I want to track my commitment-keeping consistency, so that I can see my character growth

**Out-of-the-Box Commitments:** Daily check-ins, daily phone calls, daily/weekly meetings, daily prayer/scripture, daily exercise

**Custom Commitments:** User defines what + how often, with category tagging (spiritual, physical, relational, intellectual, emotional)

**Integration:** Integrated into morning commitment and nightly review flows; broken commitments trigger reflection prompts, not shame

---

### 4.3 Activities

Activities are actions a user can take within the app. Each activity may feed into the Tracking System and appear on the calendar.

---

#### **ACTIVITY: Daily Sobriety Commitment**

**Priority:** P0 (Must-Have)

**Description:** Morning commitment ritual with accountability and evening review.

**User Stories:**
- As a **recovering user**, I want to make a daily commitment to sobriety each morning, so that I start my day with intention and accountability
- As a **recovering user**, I want to review my commitment each evening, so that I can reflect on my day and maintain honesty
- As a **recovering user**, I want to be reminded to make my commitment, so that I don't forget this critical daily practice

**Morning Commitment Questions:**

Users can enable/disable individual default questions and add custom questions via Settings → Morning Commitment.

**Default Questions (user selects which to include):**
1. "Do you admit, just for today, that you are powerless over lust and sexual acting out, and do you desire sobriety and freedom for the next 24 hours?"
2. "Will you commit, with God's help, to stay sober for the next 24 hours — abstaining from sex with yourself or anyone other than your spouse — working the SA program and its 12 steps as a tool, while recognizing that it is God, not the tool, who keeps you sober?"
3. "Do you recognize all lust hits as toxic, and are you willing to go to any lengths to protect your sobriety, including bringing any danger zones — past or upcoming — into the light?"
4. "Are you willing, just for today, to turn your will and the care of your life over to the God who kept you sober yesterday and has protected you from the full consequences of your lust in the past?"
5. "Briefly share your last 24 hours, focusing on lust, resentment, fear, and time spent with your Higher Power — and what is your recovery plan for the next 24 hours?" *(free-text response)*
6. "What is one thing in your recovery for which you are grateful or proud?" *(free-text response)*

**Custom Questions:** Yes/No affirmation, free-text response, or scale (1-5)

**Morning Commitment Flow:**
1. Commitment Prompt Screen (headline, questions, motivations display, "Make My Commitment" / "I'm Struggling Today")
2. Commitment Confirmation Screen (animation, streak display, today's verse/affirmation)
3. "I'm Struggling Today" Flow (crisis contacts, urge logging, motivations review, affirmations)

**Evening Commitment Review Questions:**
1. "Did you keep your commitment to sobriety today?" (required, always shown) — Yes / Struggled / Acted Out
2. "What are you grateful for today?"
3. "What did you learn today?"
4. "What's one thing you'll do differently tomorrow?"

**Evening Commitment Review Flow:**
1. Review Prompt Screen with sobriety status question first
2. Tomorrow's Preparation with optional calendar integration

**Interaction Specifications:**
- Push notification at user-set time (default 8:00 AM morning, 9:00 PM evening)
- Snooze option: 15 minutes (max 3 times)
- Milestone celebrations at standard intervals
- Streak reset policy: Only resets if user intentionally skips

---

#### **ACTIVITY: Affirmations**

**Priority:** P0 (Must-Have)

**Description:** Scripture-based affirmations library (50+) with daily delivery, custom creation, and on-demand access.

**User Stories:**
- As a **recovering user**, I want to receive daily Christian affirmations, so that I can stay spiritually grounded
- As a **recovering user**, I want to create custom affirmations, so that I can personalize encouragement
- As a **recovering user**, I want affirmations tied to scripture, so that my faith and recovery are integrated

**Affirmation Delivery:** Daily push notification, integrated into morning flow, post-urge log, on-demand access

**Affirmation Structure:** First-person statement (present tense), scripture reference, optional expansion, optional prayer

**Affirmation Packs:**
- Freemium: Basic Affirmations Pack (50+ across 5 categories)
- Premium: Additional themed packs (unlocked forever when purchased)

**Affirmation Selection Modes:**
1. Individually Chosen — manual selection from owned packs
2. Random Automatic — system randomly selects from owned packs
3. Package Mode — Permanent Package or Day-of-Week Package

**Custom Affirmation Creation:** Statement, scripture, category/tag, display schedule

**Rotation Logic:** Weighted by triggers (40%), favorites (30%), under-served categories (20%), random (10%); contextual triggers always override mode

---

#### **ACTIVITY: Urge Logging & Emergency Tools**

**Priority:** P0 (Must-Have)

**Description:** Log urges, trigger emergency coping toolkit.

**User Stories:**
- As a **recovering user**, I want to quickly log an urge when triggered, so that I can interrupt the craving cycle
- As a **recovering user**, I want to identify triggers, so that I can recognize patterns
- As a **recovering user**, I want immediate access to healthy coping activities
- As a **recovering user**, I want to send a quick help signal to my support network

**Quick Access:** Emergency FAB on every screen, Dashboard widget, Lock Screen widget, voice command

**Urge Logging Flow (4 screens max):**
1. Intensity & Addiction (slider 1-10, addiction selection)
2. Trigger Identification (quick-select chips: Emotional, Environmental, Relational, Physical, Digital, Spiritual, Other)
3. Context Notes (optional, 1000 chars, voice-to-text)
4. Action Plan (contact support, healthy activities, recovery tools)
5. Urge Resolution ("Did you maintain sobriety?")

**Urge History View:** Summary dashboard, trend graph, insights, reverse chronological log with filters, pattern analysis (heatmap, trigger breakdown, correlation insights)

**Emergency Tools Overlay:** Crisis contacts, 5-minute breathing timer, GPS to safe locations, Panic Prayer, Accountability Broadcast, Temptation Timer / Urge Surfing Tool, distraction tools

**Temptation Timer / Urge Surfing Tool:**

A live-event intervention tool for acute urges that makes the urge feel finite and survivable by visualizing the physiological reality that most urges peak and pass within 15-20 minutes.

- **Activation:** From Emergency Tools overlay, Urge Log action plan, or standalone from Tools navigation
- **Visual:** Large animated wave that rises, peaks, and falls over a 20-minute cycle — the user "surfs" the wave. Their position on the wave moves forward in real-time.
- **Timer display:** Elapsed time prominently shown: "You've resisted for 4 minutes. Most urges pass in 15. You're almost there."
- **Milestone markers on the wave:** 5 minutes ("The hardest part is starting"), 10 minutes ("You're past the peak — it gets easier from here"), 15 minutes ("Almost through — the urge is fading"), 20 minutes ("You made it.")
- **Recovery data overlay:** During the timer, the screen shows rotating motivations, current sobriety streak, and a family photo (if uploaded)
- **Companion tools accessible during the timer:** Breathing exercise button (overlays breathing guide on the wave animation), Prayer button (opens a contextual prayer without leaving the timer), Call sponsor button (one-tap dial without closing the timer)
- **Completion:** At 20 minutes (or when user taps "I'm okay now" at any point), celebration: "You rode the wave. This urge could not defeat you." Urge automatically logged with outcome "Resisted" and duration.
- **Historical impact display:** "You've successfully surfed X urges. Your average ride-out time is Y minutes. It gets shorter over time."
- **Works fully offline** — no server dependency
- **Haptic feedback:** Optional gentle pulse every 60 seconds as a grounding rhythm

**Technical Notes:** All emergency tools work fully offline; all actions load in <1 second

---

#### **ACTIVITY: Journaling**

**Priority:** P0

**Description:** Structured and free-form journaling with multiple modes.

**User Stories:**
- As a recovering user, I want to journal my thoughts and feelings, so that I can process emotions healthily
- As a recovering user, I want quick bullet-style jotting for brief thoughts
- As a recovering user, I want journal prompts, so that I know what to write about

**Journaling Modes:**
1. **Jotting** — bullet points, lightweight
2. **Journaling** — Free-form, Free-form with Prompts (100+), Structured (guided template)

**Features:** Voice-to-text, emotional tagging, daily prompt notification, searchable entries, export to PDF, feeds into Tracking System

---

#### **ACTIVITY: Recovery Check-ins**

**Priority:** P1

**Description:** Daily self-assessment questionnaire with scoring, trends, and configurable questions.

**User Stories:**
- As a **recovering user**, I want daily check-ins to assess my recovery health, so that I stay aware of my status
- As a **recovering user**, I want to see my check-in scores over time, so that I can identify patterns and progress
- As a **recovering user**, I want to customize my check-in questions, so that they reflect my specific recovery goals

**Default Check-in Questions (5-7):** Sobriety status, urge count, meeting attendance, spiritual practices, emotional state, support network contact, overall recovery health rating

**Scoring:** 0-100 scale, weighted (sobriety + urges weighted higher), color-coded (Green/Yellow/Orange/Red)

**Trends & Insights:** Line graph views, per-question breakdown, weekly summary, correlation insights, alerts for sustained low scores

**Check-in Types:** Daily Check-in and FASTER Scale Check-in

---

#### **ACTIVITY: Spouse Check-in Preparation**

**Priority:** P1

**Description:** Structured preparation tool for couples check-in conversations using FANOS or FITNAP frameworks.

**User Stories:**
- As a **recovering user**, I want a guided framework for checking in with my spouse, so that our conversations are structured and healing
- As a **recovering user**, I want to prepare my thoughts before a spouse check-in, so that I communicate with intentionality and care

**Framework: FANOS** — Feelings (with Feelings Wheel), Appreciation, Needs, Ownership, Success

**Framework: FITNAP** — Feelings (with early memory identification), Integrity (sobriety update), Triggers (hold space for spouse), Needs, Amends, Positives

**Check-in Flow:** Select framework, guided prompts per section, Feelings Wheel reference, voice-to-text, review screen, save to history

---

#### **ACTIVITY: Guided 12 Step Work**

**Priority:** P2

**Description:** Step work tracking and guided exercises.

**User Stories:**
- As a recovering user, I want to work through the 12 steps with guided exercises, so that I can deepen my recovery work
- As a recovering user, I want to share my step work with my sponsor, so that I can receive feedback and accountability

**Summary:** Supports SA (with AA supporting materials) and Celebrate Recovery. Each step has explanation, reflection questions (10-15), worksheets, prayer, milestone celebration. Progress tracker, sponsor collaboration, PDF export, feeds into Tracking System.

---

#### **ACTIVITY: Personal Craziness Index (PCI)**

**Priority:** P2

**Description:** 10 custom activities that are tracked and create a daily score (from Patrick Carnes).

**User Stories:**
- As a recovering user, I want to track warning signs that I'm moving toward relapse
- As a recovering user, I want to share my PCI with my sponsor for accountability

**Summary:** User defines 10 personal warning behaviors, daily check marks, score calculated, alerts at elevated scores, historical tracking.

---

#### **ACTIVITY: FASTER Scale**

**Priority:** P1

**Description:** Self-assessment tool based on Michael Dye's FASTER Scale.

**User Stories:**
- As a recovering user, I want to assess where I am on the FASTER Scale, so that I can catch myself sliding toward relapse before it happens
- As a recovering user, I want to track my FASTER Scale results over time, so that I can see patterns and share them with my sponsor or counselor

**FASTER Scale Stages:**
1. F — Forgetting Priorities
2. A — Anxiety
3. S — Speeding Up
4. T — Ticked Off
5. E — Exhausted
6. R — Relapse (redirects to Post-Mortem and Relapse Logging)

**Scoring & Alerts:** Green (Restoration), Yellow (F/A), Orange (S/T), Red (E), Relapse (R → logging flows)

**Integration:** Standalone or Recovery Check-in type, shareable, historical tracking, correlation analysis, feeds into Tracking System and Analytics Dashboard

---

#### **ACTIVITY: Emotional Journaling**

**Priority:** P1

**Description:** Structured journaling focused on identifying, expressing, and processing emotions healthily.

**User Stories:**
- As a recovering user, I want to identify and name my emotions in a structured way, so that I develop emotional awareness
- As a recovering user, I want to track my emotional patterns over time, so that I can see growth in my emotional health

**Entry Fields:**
1. What emotion? — Feelings Wheel or emoji picker
2. Why? — Free-text (voice-to-text available)
3. Intensity — Slider 1-10 (range allows -1 to 15 for extremes)

Multiple entries per day allowed. Tracks patterns over time. Feeds into Tracking System.

---

#### **ACTIVITY: Meetings Attended**

**Priority:** P1

**Description:** Log meeting attendance with optional notes.

---

##### User Stories

- As a **recovering user**, I want to log each recovery meeting I attend, so that I can track my consistency and commitment to community-based recovery
- As a **recovering user**, I want to categorize meetings by type (12-step, therapy, church, etc.), so that I can see which forms of support I'm engaging with most
- As a **recovering user**, I want to add notes after a meeting, so that I can capture key takeaways, feelings, or action items while they're fresh
- As a **recovering user**, I want to see my meeting attendance history over time, so that I can identify patterns between attendance and my overall recovery health
- As a **sponsor**, I want to see whether my sponsee is attending meetings regularly, so that I can encourage consistency or address gaps early
- As a **recovering user**, I want meeting attendance to count toward my commitments and streaks, so that I'm motivated to keep showing up
- As a **recovering user**, I want to quickly log a meeting with minimal effort, so that tracking doesn't feel like a burden on top of recovery work

---

##### Summary

- **Quick-log entry fields:**
  - Which meeting (name or group — free text or saved favorites)
  - Meeting type: 12-step (SA, AA, Celebrate Recovery), therapy session, group counseling, church, custom
  - Date and time
  - Duration (optional)
  - Notes (optional — free text, voice-to-text available)

- **Saved Meetings:** Users can save frequently attended meetings (name, type, day/time, location) for one-tap logging in the future

- **Attendance History:**
  - Browse past meetings by date
  - Filter by meeting type
  - View monthly/weekly attendance counts
  - Tap any past entry to see full details and notes

- **Integration Points:**
  - Feeds into Tracking System (consecutive days/weeks of meeting attendance based on user's commitment frequency)
  - Feeds into Commitments tracking (if user has a "attend X meetings per week" commitment)
  - Visible to support network (sponsor, counselor, coach) based on community permissions
  - Appears on calendar view in the Tracking System
  - Correlates with Analytics Dashboard (e.g., "Your sobriety score averages 12 points higher on weeks you attend 3+ meetings")

- **Notifications:**
  - Optional reminder before saved meeting times
  - Post-meeting prompt: "You had a meeting scheduled today. Would you like to log it?" (if not already logged)

- **Edge Cases:**
  - Multiple meetings in one day → Each logged independently
  - User attends a meeting type not in the default list → "Custom" type with free-text label
  - Meeting canceled → User can mark as "Canceled" to preserve the record without breaking commitment streaks (configurable: user chooses whether cancellations count or not)
  - Offline logging → Saved locally, synced when connection restored

---

#### **ACTIVITY: Post-Mortem Analysis**

**Priority:** P1

**Description:** Structured review of the entire last 24 hours after a relapse or near-miss event, tracing the full progression from normalcy to acting out.

---

##### User Stories

- As a **recovering user**, I want to walk through the full 24 hours leading up to a relapse, so that I can understand the chain of events, emotions, and decisions that led me there
- As a **recovering user**, I want to identify the specific decision points where I could have intervened, so that I can build a concrete plan for next time
- As a **recovering user**, I want to map my FASTER Scale stages onto the timeline, so that I can recognize how far I had progressed toward relapse before I noticed
- As a **recovering user**, I want to see a visual timeline of my progression, so that the pattern becomes clear and memorable rather than abstract
- As a **recovering user**, I want to create an action plan from my analysis, so that I leave with specific changes I can implement immediately
- As a **recovering user**, I want to share my completed post-mortem with my sponsor or counselor, so that we can discuss it together and strengthen my recovery plan
- As a **recovering user**, I want to review past post-mortems, so that I can spot recurring patterns across multiple relapses and address root causes
- As a **recovering user**, I want the post-mortem process to feel compassionate rather than punishing, so that I engage with it honestly instead of avoiding it out of shame
- As a **sponsor**, I want to see my sponsee's post-mortem analysis, so that I can help them identify blind spots and reinforce healthier decision-making

---

##### Guided Walkthrough Sections

The post-mortem guides the user through a structured reconstruction of their day, broken into six sections:

##### 1. The Day Before
- What was your emotional and spiritual state going into the day?
- Had you been keeping up with your recovery practices?
- Were there any unresolved conflicts, stressors, or unmet needs?
- Free-text input with optional mood rating (1-10)

##### 2. Morning
- How did the day start? Did you complete your morning commitment?
- What was your mood when you woke up?
- Did anything notable happen in the first few hours?
- Auto-populated data (if available): morning commitment completion status, mood rating, affirmation viewed

##### 3. Throughout the Day
- Walk through key events, interactions, and emotional shifts hour by hour
- Guided time-block prompts (morning, midday, afternoon, evening) or free-form hour-by-hour entry
- For each block: What were you doing? Where were you? Who were you with? What were you thinking and feeling?
- Identify when warning signs first appeared (FASTER Scale stages, PCI behaviors, acting-in behaviors)

##### 4. The Build-Up
- When did you first notice something was off?
- What triggers accumulated? (link to trigger categories from Urge Logging: Emotional, Environmental, Relational, Physical, Digital, Spiritual)
- What did you do — or not do — in response?
- Were there moments you considered reaching out for help but didn't? Why?
- Decision point identification: "At this moment, I could have _____ but instead I _____"

##### 5. The Acting Out
